30:843:64877:7:39:323:498:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:), suggests that the effect on college 
30:844:64916:39:12:89:524:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:                                                                                                                                                 
30:845:65060:12:11:89:493:153:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:derived from the Pupil-Teacher Ratio reported in Table 24. The specifications used to estimate these 
30:846:65161:11:7:89:495:142:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:numbers include state and year effects; adding state specific trends had little impact on the estimates. 
30:847:65266:7:16:125:523:135:6:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:29 The dependent variable is the share of college graduates in each state and birth cohort, measured 
30:848:65367:16:12:89:495:119:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:in logarithmic form. Pupil-teacher measures were provided by Alan Krueger and reflect the potential 
30:849:65467:12:0:89:497:107:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:resources available to students in the K-12 years. All regressions include state and year fixed effects.  
31:850:65575:0:28:89:519:709:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:completion operating through resources is likely to be quite modest (0.07 to 0.08). While 
31:851:65665:28:28:89:509:681:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:demand-side effects are plainly not zero, and the impact of cohort size on precollegiate 
31:852:65754:28:27:89:519:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:academic achievement is an interesting question in its own right, these effects are plainly 
31:853:65846:27:28:89:459:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:too small to explain the entire effect of cohort size or resources on collegiate 
31:854:65927:28:27:89:154:598:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:attainment.31 
31:855:65940:27:28:125:475:571:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Some additional evidence indicates that the cohort size effect on college 
31:856:66014:28:28:89:493:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:preparedness is not the major factor behind the strong negative association between 
31:857:66098:28:27:89:506:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:college completion rates and cohort size. Using data from the College Board’s Annual 
31:858:66183:27:28:89:513:488:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:Survey of Colleges, which includes institution-level characteristics of the undergraduate 
31:859:66273:28:27:89:511:460:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:class and admission process from 1986-2000, we found that a 10% increase in a within-
31:860:66358:27:28:89:493:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:state cohort size was associated with a roughly 1.1 (0.4) percentage point rise in the 
31:861:66445:28:28:89:472:405:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:fraction of college students with a GPA of 3.0 or better, and a 2.9 /2.7 (0.8/0.7) 
31:862:66528:28:27:89:487:377:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:percentage point rise in verbal/math SAT scores.  Given problems with these data, 
31:863:66610:27:28:89:512:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:including considerable missing data and a relatively short time horizon, we do not want 
31:864:66698:28:27:89:511:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to overemphasize these results, but they are certainly consistent with the notion that the 
31:865:66789:27:28:89:488:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:dominant factor effecting the negative association between cohort size and college 
31:866:66872:28:28:89:504:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:completion rates is educational crowding out rather than lack of college preparedness. 
31:867:66959:28:27:89:92:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: 
31:868:66959:27:8:89:524:212:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:                                                                                                                                                 
31:869:67103:8:16:125:504:204:6:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:30 See Loeb and Bound (1996) for a more extensive discussion of this issue. In similar fashion 
31:870:67198:16:11:89:497:188:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:Hanushek, Rivkin and Taylor (1996) argue that state level aggregation is likely to exacerbate omitted 
31:871:67300:11:7:89:330:177:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:variable bias, leading to an overstatement of causal effects.  
31:872:67363:7:16:125:514:170:6:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:31 An alternative way to measure the effects of cohort size on college preparedness is to measure 
31:873:67461:16:12:89:519:154:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:the effect of cohort size on test scores directly. Unfortunately, NAEP scores provide only a limited number 
31:874:67569:12:11:89:494:142:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:of state-specific observations over time. SAT scores at the state level may suffer from changes in the 
31:875:67672:11:12:89:514:131:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:selection of the test-taking population over time. Using data on SAT scores at the state level from 1971 to 
31:876:67780:12:11:89:479:119:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:2000, regressions of test scores on the log of cohort size with state and year fixed effects yields a 
31:877:67882:11:12:89:499:108:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:coefficient of -43.27  (18.12), implying that a 10% increase in cohort size would lead to a within-state 
31:878:67987:12:11:89:520:96:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:decrease in scores of less than 4.5 points overall.  These effects are modest in magnitude, though indicative 
31:879:68097:11:0:89:523:85:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:of some reduction in college-preparedness with cohort size. More surprising is the link between the share of 
32:880:68208:0:13:89:163:708:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f4:V. Conclusion 
32:881:68221:13:14:89:92:695:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4: 
32:882:68221:14:28:125:516:681:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In this paper we have documented substantial cohort crowding effects on college 
32:883:68301:28:27:89:513:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:completion rates – our estimates suggest that a 10% state specific increase in the size of 
32:884:68392:27:28:89:511:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the college age population leads to a 4% decline in the fraction attaining a BA.  Neither 
32:885:68482:28:27:89:498:598:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:growth in out-of-state enrollment nor expansion of private enrollment is sufficient to 
32:886:68569:27:28:89:507:571:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:“absorb” the effects of cohort size on enrollment and attainment at public colleges and 
32:887:68657:28:28:89:521:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:universities. The available evidence suggests that this crowding out effect occurs because 
32:888:68748:28:27:89:492:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:public colleges are unable to absorb the increased demand for college education, as 
32:889:68832:27:28:89:501:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:public resources do not increase sufficiently. While it might seem plausible that large 
32:890:68920:28:27:89:520:460:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:cohorts would reach college age less well prepared to continue their education than small 
32:891:69010:27:28:89:514:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:cohorts, our estimates suggest that neither the effects of declines in school quality in the 
32:892:69103:28:28:89:519:405:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:elementary and secondary years nor the effects of changes in the composition of the pool 
32:893:69192:28:27:89:500:377:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of potential college students associated with large cohorts are  nearly large enough to 
32:894:69280:27:28:89:520:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:produce the observed negative relationship between cohort size and college completion.   
32:895:69369:28:27:125:518:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:On the supply side of the market, the reduction in college completion with cohort 
32:896:69451:27:28:89:491:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:size occurs on two margins. Among institutions, those with the greatest non-tuition 
32:897:69535:28:28:89:482:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:resources per student, such as flagship universities, are the least likely to increase 
32:898:69622:28:27:89:496:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:enrollment to accommodate relatively large cohorts; still, these universities have the 
32:899:69709:27:28:89:500:212:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:highest levels of college completion. To the extent that the distribution of enrollment 
32:900:69797:28:27:89:506:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:shifts away from these resource-intensive institutions, the college completion rate will 
32:901:69886:27:59:89:498:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:fall. Within public institutions, those that expand to meet population-related shifts in 
32:902:69975:59:12:89:524:98:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:                                                                                                                                                 
32:903:70119:12:12:89:514:86:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:eligible seniors taking the exam and cohort size, which is positive and significant. One explanation is that 
32:904:70228:12:0:89:419:74:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:colleges increase requirements for standardized tests with relatively large cohorts. 
33:905:70315:0:28:89:497:709:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:demand may face reductions in resources per student, further reducing attainment of 
33:906:70399:28:28:89:180:681:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:enrolled students.  
33:907:70419:28:27:125:518:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:While it is plain that the well-known cyclical variation in state funding for higher 
33:908:70504:27:28:89:517:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:education may have deleterious effects on public colleges and universities, it is the more 
33:909:70595:28:27:89:509:598:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sustained depletion in resources per student accompanying relatively large cohorts that 
33:910:70683:27:28:89:503:571:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:has the significant impact on collegiate attainment and the supply of college-educated 
33:911:70770:28:28:89:516:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:workers to the economy. In the coming decade, many states are facing large increases in 
33:912:70858:28:27:89:515:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the college-age population, with serious questions about the capacity of state colleges to 
33:913:70949:27:28:89:499:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:meet enrollment demand for these cohorts.32 Adding to the demographic pressure on 
33:914:71031:28:27:89:507:460:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:higher education resources created by increasing cohort size are persistently tight state 
33:915:71121:27:28:89:522:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:budget circumstances in which higher education competes with entitlement programs and 
33:916:71207:28:28:89:393:405:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the rising cost of healthcare (Kane, Orszag, and Gunter, 2003). 
33:917:71271:28:27:125:508:377:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The impending collision of large cohorts and limited public resources in higher 
33:918:71351:27:28:89:512:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:education is not just a predicament for colleges and universities, but a potential crisis in 
33:919:71444:28:27:89:497:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:economic growth for decades to come if the flow of college-educated workers to the 
33:920:71527:27:28:89:479:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:labor force is further curtailed. Because tuition is a small enough part of the total 
33:921:71613:28:28:89:513:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:revenues of higher education, it would take enormous increases in tuition to provide the 
33:922:71702:28:27:89:504:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:necessary resources for colleges and universities to expand and maintain quality, with 
33:923:71789:27:28:89:512:212:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:such a shift adversely affecting the level and distribution of enrollment. At issue is how 
33:924:71880:28:27:89:511:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:colleges and universities, particularly in the public sector, can raise resources from non-
33:925:71971:27:37:89:503:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:tuition sources to expand the pool of collegiate opportunities without diluting quality. 
33:926:72060:37:7:89:236:120:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:                                                 
33:927:72108:7:16:125:512:113:6:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:32 For example one report estimated that the number of students seeking to enroll at California’s 
33:928:72206:16:11:89:500:97:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:public colleges would rise by 36% between 2000 and 2010. Former University of California President 
33:929:72305:11:12:89:508:86:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:Clark Kerr has dubbed this projected increase in demand “Tidal Wave II” as nearly three-quarters of the 
33:930:72409:12:0:89:403:74:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:projected growth is strictly attributable to population growth (Schmidt, 1999). 
34:931:72491:0:28:89:514:709:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:While states have, historically, been central to the development of infrastructure and the 
34:932:72582:28:28:89:504:681:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:provision of subsidy in higher education, the current fiscal constraints and restrictions 
34:933:72672:28:27:89:502:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:against deficit funding may limit the capacity of states to make investments in human 
34:934:72758:27:27:89:324:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:capital through public colleges and universities.

43:1257:83774:12:13:89:511:312:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:institution-level data from the HEGIS/IPEDs.   Enrollment data are aligned with the population 
43:1258:83869:13:12:89:510:299:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:age 18 in the state in the concurrent year; BA data are aligned with the population age 18 years 
43:1259:83966:12:13:89:500:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:old in the state 4 years prior, in accordance with the expectation of a four-year modal time to 
43:1260:84062:13:13:89:507:274:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:degree.  See Data Appendix for further details.  Each entry and associated standard error is the 
43:1261:84159:13:12:89:512:261:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:coefficient on the log of the population measure in a regression that also includes state and year 
43:1262:84258:12:0:89:149:249:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:fixed effects. 
44:1263:84275:0:13:89:91:710:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3: 
44:1264:84275:13:14:89:170:697:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Data Appendix 
44:1265:84289:14:13:89:92:683:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: 
44:1266:84289:13:14:89:518:670:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: The primary sources of data for this analysis are: institutional surveys of colleges 
44:1267:84374:14:14:89:471:656:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and universities, the decennial Census files, the decennial Census publications, 
44:1268:84455:14:14:89:495:642:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:population estimates by the Census Bureau, and standard measures of labor markets 
44:1269:84537:14:14:89:167:628:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f4:characteristics.  
44:1270:84554:14:14:89:92:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: 
44:1271:84554:14:13:89:174:600:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Population data 
44:1272:84570:13:14:89:92:587:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4: 
44:1273:84570:14:14:89:512:573:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3: Population measures by state and age are primary to our analysis. There are two 
44:1274:84650:14:14:89:515:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sources for our population measures: age-specific estimates from the Census bureau and 
44:1275:84737:14:14:89:407:545:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:measures of birth cohort size from the Vital Statistics tabulations. 
44:1276:84806:14:13:89:92:531:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4: 
44:1277:84806:13:14:89:515:518:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3: Measures of birth cohort size for each state from 1928 – 1975 were entered from 
44:1278:84886:14:14:89:510:504:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:vital statistics data distributed by the National Center for Health Statistics. The original 
44:1279:84979:14:14:89:487:490:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:data came from birth registrations. (These are the cohorts that would have been 22 
44:1280:85062:14:14:89:213:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:between 1950 and 1997). 
44:1281:85086:14:13:89:92:462:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4: 
44:1282:85086:13:14:125:513:449:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:For the most recent three decades, data on population by state and single year of 
44:1283:85168:14:14:89:488:435:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:age are available through the Bureau of the Census website. For the years between 
44:1284:85250:14:14:89:519:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Census enumerations, these numbers are estimates which take into account mortality and 
44:1285:85337:14:13:89:485:407:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:migration. See: http://eire.census.gov/popest/topics/methodology/stage98.txt for a 
44:1286:85420:13:14:89:516:394:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:discussion of this methodology. For the years before 1970, we combine data on the state 
44:1287:85508:14:14:89:518:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and single year of age enumerations published in the U.S. Census Bureau State Volumes 
44:1288:85594:14:14:89:502:366:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:for 1950 (Table 51), 1960 (Table 94), and 1970 (Table 19) and the total population in 
44:1289:85680:14:14:89:507:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:each state and year for single years from 1950-1970. Because the population measures 
44:1290:85765:14:13:89:505:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:between census enumerations are estimates, measurement error is a logical concern as 
44:1291:85850:13:14:89:195:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:discussed in the text.  
44:1292:85874:14:14:89:92:311:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4: 
44:1293:85874:14:14:89:319:297:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:College enrollment and BA degree outcomes 
44:1294:85916:14:14:89:92:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: 
44:1295:85916:14:13:89:518:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: The primary measures of collegiate attainment are collected from federal surveys 
44:1296:85997:13:14:89:506:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of colleges and universities. The degree data are based on the annual “Earned Degrees 
44:1297:86083:14:14:89:505:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Conferred” survey conducted by the National Center for Education Statistics (NCES), 
44:1298:86167:14:14:89:515:228:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:which records degrees awarded in the 12-month academic year from July to June.33 The 
44:1299:86252:14:14:89:494:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:enrollment data are from the “Fall Enrollment” surveys which record the number of 
44:1300:86334:14:13:89:494:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:students enrolled in classes in the fall. Through 1986, these surveys were part of the 
44:1301:86421:13:14:89:483:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:larger NCES Higher Education General Information Survey (HEGIS), which was 
44:1302:86496:14:14:89:480:173:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:subsequently redesigned as the Integrated Postsecondary Education Data System 
44:1303:86574:14:14:89:187:159:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(IPEDS) collection. 
44:1304:86594:14:36:89:92:145:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: 
44:1305:86594:36:8:89:236:109:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:                                                 
44:1306:86642:8:15:125:489:101:6:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:33 In 1960-61, the survey began to separately delineate first professional and baccalaureate 
44:1307:86735:15:12:89:512:86:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:degrees. Prior to this point, the two were combined, reflecting the fact that in the early part of the century 
44:1308:86846:12:0:89:489:74:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:first professional programs were concurrently undergraduate degree programs at some institutions.  
45:1309:86947:0:14:125:518:709:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Historical data (primarily in the years prior to 1966) were entered from published 
45:1310:87030:14:14:89:506:695:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:tabulations in the government document publications under the titles “Earned Degrees 
45:1311:87115:14:14:89:508:681:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Conferred” and “Opening Fall Enrollment.” Machine-readable data are employed after 
45:1312:87198:14:14:89:502:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:1966 (1967 for enrollment), which allows for the distinction of institutions by control 
45:1313:87286:14:13:89:305:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(public/private) and Carnegie Classification. 
45:1314:87332:13:14:125:128:640:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: 
45:1315:87332:14:14:125:480:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Another source of data from institutional collections is the Residence and 
45:1316:87407:14:14:89:483:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Migration Survey conducted periodically by the Office of Education and later the 
45:1317:87488:14:14:89:512:598:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Department of Education. Data for the following years are available: 1949, 1958, 1963, 
45:1318:87575:14:13:89:499:584:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:1968, 1972, 1975, 1979, 1981, 1984, 1986, 1988, 1992, 1994, and 1996. This survey 
45:1319:87657:13:14:89:494:571:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:records first-time freshman enrollment by state of residence and state of attendance. 
45:1320:87743:14:14:89:92:557:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: 
45:1321:87743:14:14:125:519:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In addition to the data which record degrees awarded and enrollment in each year 
45:1322:87824:14:14:89:516:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and state by colleges and universities, the decennial Census enumerations record college 
45:1323:87913:14:13:89:488:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:attainment to individuals by state of birth and age (or, implicitly, year of birth). As 
45:1324:88001:13:14:89:524:502:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:discussed in the text, the Census data are conceptually different from the institutional data 
45:1325:88095:14:14:89:512:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in that they do not record the year or state of degree receipt. As is well known, the form 
45:1326:88186:14:14:89:502:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of the Census question on educational attainment changed to a degree-based question 
45:1327:88270:14:14:89:512:460:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:from an item that recorded years of attainment with the 1990 Census. When we employ 
45:1328:88354:14:13:89:521:446:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:data from the 1970 and 1980 enumerations, we treat completing 16 years as equivalent to 
45:1329:88442:13:14:89:182:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:BA degree receipt. 
45:1330:88461:14:14:89:92:419:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: 
45:1331:88461:14:14:89:271:405:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Higher education finance variables 
45:1332:88496:14:14:89:92:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: 
45:1333:88496:14:13:125:520:377:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Each year as part of the institutional reporting to the federal government, colleges 
45:1334:88581:13:14:89:502:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and universities complete a survey of institutional finances in which they report basic 
45:1335:88669:14:14:89:492:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:income and expense items, including the sources of revenues and expenses. We are 
45:1336:88750:14:14:89:503:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:particularly interested in distinguishing sources of public support from tuition and fee 
45:1337:88839:14:14:89:485:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:revenue, while also measuring the total level of educational expenditures. For this 
45:1338:88923:14:13:89:354:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:purpose, we focus on the state appropriations variable. 
45:1339:88979:13:14:125:128:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: 
45:1340:88979:14:14:125:493:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:State appropriations are those monies received from or made available to an 
45:1341:89055:14:14:89:506:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:institution through acts of the state legislative body, except institutional fees and other 
45:1342:89147:14:14:89:517:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:income reappropriated by the legislatures to the institution (i.e. tuition and fees collected 
45:1343:89241:14:13:89:478:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:by the institution and returned to the institution in the form of appropriations are 
45:1344:89326:13:14:89:522:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:subtracted as they already appear as tuition and fees). This line item also includes Federal 
45:1345:89419:14:14:89:493:212:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:aid received through State channels and regional compacts.  We have compared the 
45:1346:89500:14:14:89:469:198:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:measures of state appropriations with data reported from state governments on 
45:1347:89578:14:14:89:479:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:appropriations and found these measures to be highly correlated. Data from state 
45:1348:89659:14:13:89:516:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:governments are compiled annually since 1960 by the Center for the Study of Education 
45:1349:89745:13:14:89:513:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Policy at Illinois State in the Grapevine series. These data differ slightly from measures 
45:1350:89836:14:14:89:493:143:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:reported by institutions in that they also include state funds to non-collegiate higher 
45:1351:89924:14:14:89:507:129:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:education institutions such as the administrative boards coordinating higher education. 
45:1352:90012:14:14:89:92:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: 
45:1353:90012:14:13:125:493:101:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Data on tuition and fees, measured as a price, are available from 1970 to the 
45:1354:90090:13:0:89:524:88:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:current year. There are two sources for these data, which provide measures that are highly 
46:1355:90183:0:14:89:497:709:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:correlated. First, the Department of Education collects data on tuition and fees at the 
46:1356:90271:14:14:89:470:695:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:institution level as part of the Institutional Characteristics section of the annual 
46:1357:90356:14:14:89:498:681:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:HEGIS/IPEDS surveys. In addition, the Washington Higher Education Coordinating 
46:1358:90435:14:14:89:521:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Board conducts an annual survey of tuition and fees at public institutions, which includes 
46:1359:90526:14:13:89:255:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:data from 1972-73 to the present.  
46:1360:90561:13:14:89:92:640:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: 
46:1361:90561:14:14:89:214:626:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Labor market variables 
46:1362:90584:14:14:89:92:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: 
46:1363:90584:14:14:125:457:598:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Labor market variables used in the analysis include the state specific 
46:1364:90655:14:13:89:482:584:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:unemployment rate, personal income and manufacturing wage bill. State-specific 
46:1365:90734:13:14:89:494:571:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:unemployment rates are available from 1970 through the Bureau of Labor Statistics 
46:1366:90816:14:14:89:500:557:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:[http://www.bls.gov/lau/staadoc.htm]. The personal income and manufacturing wage 
46:1367:90897:14:14:89:504:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:measures are from the U.S. Department of Commerce, Bureau of Economic Analysis, 
46:1368:90977:14:14:89:386:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Regional Accounts Data and are available from 1958 to 2001 
46:1369:91036:14:13:89:519:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:[http://www.bea.doc.gov/bea/regional/spi/default.cfm#s2, the manufacturing wage bill is 
46:1370:91124:13:14:89:256:502:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the s07 series, industry code 400]. 
46:1371:91160:14:14:89:92:488:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4: 
46:1372:91160:14:14:125:517:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In addition, we compute the state- and age-specific measures of the college wage 
46:1373:91241:14:14:89:486:460:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:premium in the 1970, 1980, and 1990 Census enumerations. The adjusted average 
46:1374:91319:14:13:89:523:446:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:relative wage measures are computed as the return to exactly a BA Degree (or 16 years of 
46:1375:91408:13:14:89:490:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:completed education) from state-specific hourly wage regressions with a full set of 
46:1376:91492:14:14:89:503:419:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:controls for demographic and labor force characteristics including, race, sex, and part-
46:1377:91580:14:14:89:147:405:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:time status. 
46:1378:91593:14:14:89:92:391:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4: 
46:1379:91593:14:14:89:316:377:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:Primary-secondary school quality measures 
46:1380:91635:14:13:89:92:363:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4: 
46:1381:91635:13:14:125:510:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Measures of school quality experienced for students of different states and ages 
46:1382:91716:14:14:89:512:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:are from the data assembled by Card and Krueger (1992; see Appendix A of this paper) 
46:1383:91801:14:14:89:517:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:for the analysis of the effects of school quality on earnings. The original source for these 
46:1384:91894:14:13:89:510:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:data is the Biennial Survey of Education in the United States and related materials. The 
46:1385:91983:13:14:89:505:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:specific measures employed in this analysis were the pupil-teacher ratio, average term 
46:1386:92070:14:14:89:523:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:length, and average teacher salary from academic year 1919-20 to academic year 1965-66 
46:1387:92157:14:14:89:496:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(coded by C-K as 1920-1960 for even years). To provide a single measure of school 
46:1388:92239:14:14:89:482:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:quality for each single year birth cohort, we averaged the potential school quality

46:1392:92583:14:14:89:229:198:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:expenditures and class size).
